The Secrets of Lordship and Knowledge
Ghazali presents reports and commentary on hidden knowledge and its limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali reconciles the existence of hidden spiritual secrets with the outward foundations of religion.

Core Idea
Inner knowledge complements outward religion; revealing secrets to the unfit harms both.

This passage from Ghazali's Qawaid al-Aqa'id brings together reports from early Muslims about deeper layers of knowledge that were not publicly disclosed. Some warnings even suggest that revealing these secrets could nullify prophethood or rulings. But Ghazali immediately clarifies that these statements are conditional and do not imply any contradiction with the outward religion. In this lesson, you will see how he carefully distinguishes between different audiences and circumstances, preserving the integrity of both the inner and outer dimensions of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the reports about hidden knowledge
Start with the hadith of Abu Huraira and the report about Abu Bakr's secret. Notice that the secret is related to the foundations of religion.
The secret is not outside qawa'id al-din.
2
Identify the three kinds of knowledge
Read Sahl al-Tustari's classification: outward, inner, and private. Understand that each level has its proper audience.
3
Analyze the warnings about disclosing secrets
The passage mentions strong statements: disclosing the secret of lordship is kufr, and a chain of nullifications. Ask yourself what these statements really mean.
Ghazali warns against taking them literally without context.
4
Understand the resolution
Read how Ghazali explains the conditional nullification: for the weak-minded, or due to disobedience. This preserves harmony between inner and outer.
The perfect person balances knowledge and piety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابو هريرة رضي الله عنه حفظت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وعاءين أما أحدهما فبثثته وأما الآخر لو بثثته لقطع هذا الحلقوم
وقال صلى الله عليه وسلم : « ما فضلكم أبو بكر بكثرة صيام ولا صلاة ولكن بسر وقر في صدره » رضي الله عنه
ولا شك في أن ذلك السر كان متعلقا بقواعد الدين غير خارج منها ، وما كان من قواعد الدين لم يكن خافيا بظواهره على غيره .
وقال سهل التستري رضي الله عنه : للعالم ثلاثة علوم : علم ظاهر يبذله لأهل الظاهر ، وعلم باطن لا يسعه أظهاره إلا لأهله وعلم هو بينه وبين الله تعالى لا يظهره لأحد
وقال بعض العارفين : إفشاء سر الربوبية كفر
وقال بعضهم : للربوبية سر لو أظهر لبطلت النبوة ، وللنبوة سر لو كشف بطل العلم ، وللعلماء بالله سر لو أظهروه لبطلت الأحكام
وهذا القائل إن لم يرد بذلك بطلان النبوة في حق الضعفاء لقصور فهمهم فما ذكره ليس بحق ، بل الصحيح أنه لا تناقض فيه ، وأن الكامل من لا يطفىء نور معرفته نور ورعه وملاك الورع النبوة
وسر الالوهية الذي بمعرفته يستحق النبوة من وصل إلى الله باليقين الذي لولاه لم يكن نبيا لا يخلو إما أن يكون إنكشافه من الله تعالى مما يطلع على القلوب من الأنوار التي كانت غائبة عنها ، بأن كانت القلوب ضعيفة طرأ عليها من الدهش والإصطلام والحيرة والتيه ما يبهر العقول ويفقد الإحساس ، ويقطع عن الدنيا وما فيها وذلك لضعفه ، ومن انتهى إلى هذه الحالة فتبطل النبوة في حقه أن يعرفها ، أو يعقل ما جاء من قبلها إذ قد شغله عنها ما هو أعظم لديه منها ، وربما كان سبب موته لعجزه عن حمل ما يطرأ عليه
وإما أن يكون إنكشافه من عالم به على جهة الخبر عنه ، فتبطل النبوة في حق المخبر حيث نهى عن الافشاء فأفشي وأمر أن لا يتحدث فلم يفعل ، فخرج بهذه المعصية عن طاعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيها ، فلهذا قيل في ذلك بطلت النبوة في حقه بإخباره
Abu Huraira, may Allah be pleased with him, said: I memorized from the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, two vessels: as for one of them, I disseminated it; and as for the other, if I were to disseminate it, this throat would be cut. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Abu Bakr has not surpassed you by much fasting or prayer, but by a secret (sirr) that settled in his chest.' There is no doubt that that secret was related to the foundations of the religion (qawa'id al-din), not outside them, and whatever was from the foundations of the religion was not hidden in its outward aspects from others. And Sahl al-Tustari, may Allah be pleased with him, said: For the scholar there are three kinds of knowledge: outward knowledge (zahir) which he gives to the people of the outward, inner knowledge (batin) which he cannot reveal except to its people, and knowledge which is between him and Allah Almighty, which he does not reveal to anyone. And some of the knowers (al-'arifin) said: Disclosing the secret of lordship (sirr al-rububiyya) is disbelief (kufr). And some of them said: For lordship there is a secret which, if manifested, would nullify prophethood; and for prophethood there is a secret which, if uncovered, would nullify knowledge; and for the scholars of Allah there is a secret which, if they manifested it, would nullify the rulings. This speaker, if he did not intend by that the nullification of prophethood with respect to the weak due to the deficiency of their understanding, then what he mentioned is not correct; rather, the correct view is that there is no contradiction in it, and that the perfect one is he who does not extinguish the light of his knowledge with the light of his piety (wara'), and the mainstay of piety is prophethood. The secret of divinity (sirr al-uluhiyya) by the knowledge of which one deserves prophethood—for whoever reaches Allah with certainty, without which he would not have been a prophet—is not free from either: it is either its disclosure from Allah Almighty by way of what He causes to appear in the hearts of lights that were absent from them, such that the hearts are weak and are overtaken by bewilderment, stupefaction, perplexity, and confusion that dazzle intellects, deprive sensation, and cut off from the world and what is in it—this due to weakness. Whoever reaches this state, prophethood becomes void for him in terms of knowing it or understanding what came before it, for he is preoccupied from it by what is greater for him than it, and perhaps it becomes a cause of his death due to his inability to bear what overtakes him. Or it is its disclosure from one who knows it by way of reporting it; then prophethood becomes void for the reporter, since he was forbidden from disclosure but disclosed, and commanded not to speak but did so. Thus he exits, through this disobedience, from obedience to the Prophet, peace be upon him, in that matter. For this reason it was said: prophethood became void for him due to his reporting.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a collection of reports and commentary establishing that there are deeper aspects of religious knowledge (batin) that should not be disclosed to those incapable of understanding, and that these do not contradict the outward law (zahir). The author begins with a hadith from Abu Huraira about two vessels of knowledge—one he disseminated, the other would have caused harm if revealed—and a hadith about Abu Bakr's special secret. He then comments that this secret is part of the foundations of religion (qawa'id al-din) and not hidden in its outward aspects. Next, he quotes Sahl al-Tustari's classification of three sciences: outward, inner, and secret between the scholar and Allah. Then come stronger warnings: 'Disclosing the secret of lordship is kufr' and a chain of secrets: the secret of lordship if revealed would nullify prophethood, the secret of prophethood would nullify knowledge, and the secret of knowledge would nullify rulings. The author then clarifies: if the intent is that these secrets would nullify prophethood for the weak-minded due to deficiency, then the statement is wrong. The correct view is that there is no contradiction. The perfect person does not let the light of his knowledge extinguish the light of his piety, and the mainstay of piety is prophethood. He then explains two ways the secret of divinity might cause nullification of prophethood: (1) if the revelation comes from Allah directly and overwhelms a weak heart, causing loss of normal function, then that person cannot exercise prophethood; (2) if the secret is disclosed by a knower who disobeys the command to conceal it, then he incurs disobedience and loses his prophetic quality. Thus the apparent warnings are not literal contradictions but conditional explanations.

Misconception: Some believe that inner spiritual knowledge (batin) contradicts the outward law (shari'a) and that revealing secrets always leads to heresy.
Correction: Ghazali clarifies that such secrets are within the foundations of religion and do not contradict outward aspects; warnings apply only to those unfit to hear them or to those who disobey commands of concealment.

Checkpoint

B) It refers only to revealing such secrets to those incapable of understanding them, not an absolute prohibition.
C) It means the inner meaning of religion contradicts the outward law.
D) It applies only to scholars, not to laypeople.

Key Takeaway
Hidden spiritual secrets are part of the religion's foundations; they must be disclosed only to those who can understand, and they do not contradict the outward law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe there is knowledge that you are not ready to receive, or does your pride tell you that you are capable of anything? Take a moment to ask Allah to protect you from seeking what He has not permitted for you.
?
Have you ever been entrusted with a secret about someone that you knew would harm them if revealed? How does that compare to the spiritual secrets Ghazali warns about? Will you commit to guarding the boundaries of sacred knowledge in your own life?
?
When you learn something profound about Allah, do you rush to share it with others to appear knowledgeable, or do you humbly weigh the capacity of your listener? Ask yourself: am I seeking knowledge to elevate myself or to draw closer to my Lord?

The Dilemma of Zahir and Batin
A student's objection on the relationship between outward and inner meanings, with a dilemma about contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the student's objection regarding the relationship between outward and inner meanings of scripture and why contradiction is unacceptable.

Core Idea
Esoteric interpretation must not contradict exoteric law.

Imam Ghazali presents a student’s objection that cuts to the heart of esoteric interpretation. The student asks: if the inner meaning (batin) contradicts the outward (zahir), does that not abrogate the law? And if it does not contradict, isn't it just the same? This objection forces us to define the harmony between scripture and spiritual reality. In this lesson, we examine the objection itself before seeing Ghazali’s answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins with 'Issue (mas’ala): If you say...' The student is presenting a hypothetical challenge to the author.
The passage ends with 'So the answer' but the full answer is on the next page.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The student presents two possibilities: (1) the batin contradicts the zahir, leading to nullification of the law (kufr); (2) the batin does not contradict the zahir, making it the same as the outward.
This is a classic logical dilemma.
3
Understand why contradiction is kufr
The student argues that if batin contradicts zahir, it means the spiritual reality (haqiqa) contradicts the law (shari'a). Since shari'a is the outward expression of truth, to claim that reality opposes it is disbelief.
This shows the high stakes of esoteric interpretation.
4
Reflect on the second possibility
If batin does not contradict zahir, then it seems identical to the outward. The student implies that there would be no real difference, so why speak of two levels?
The student expects the author to resolve this.
5
Prepare for the answer
Note that the answer is cut off. As you continue in the text, look for how Ghazali resolves this dilemma. The key is to show that batin is a deeper meaning that complements rather than contradicts the outward.
This lesson only covers the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: فإن قلت: هذه الآيات والأخبار يتطرق إليها تأويلات، فبين لنا كيفية إختلاف الظاهر والباطن، فإن الباطن إن كان مناقضا للظاهر ففيه إبطال الشرع، وهو قول من قال إن الحقيقة خلاف الشريعة، وهو كفر، لأن الشريعة عبارة عن الظاهر، والحقيقة عبارة عن الباطن، وإن كان لا يناقضه ولا يخالفه فهو هو، فالجواب
Issue (mas'ala): If you say: These verses and traditions are subject to interpretations, so explain to us the manner of difference between the outward (zahir) and the inner (batin). For if the inner contradicts the outward, it entails nullification of the law, and that is the saying of one who says that the reality (haqiqa) contradicts the shari'a—and that is disbelief (kufr)—because the shari'a is the outward and the reality is the inner. And if it does not contradict it nor oppose it, then it is the same. So the answer: ...
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is an objection (mas'ala) posed by a student to the author. The student points out that many verses and hadith are subject to esoteric interpretations (ta'wilat), and asks how we are to understand the relationship between the outward meaning (zahir) and the inner meaning (batin). The student presents a dilemma: if the batin contradicts the zahir, then it would effectively abrogate the law (shari'a), which is the position of those who claim that the spiritual reality (haqiqa) is contrary to the law—and that is kufr. On the other hand, if the batin does not contradict the zahir, then it is essentially the same, and there is no actual difference. The author begins his answer with 'فالجواب' (so the answer), but the full answer is not present in this window; it continues on the following pages. The objection clearly outlines the stakes of the discussion: the relationship between esoteric and exoteric interpretation must not be one of contradiction, or the entire legal framework collapses. The answer presumably resolves this by showing that batin does not contradict zahir but rather complements it.

Correction: The student's objection shows that contradiction is unacceptable because it would nullify the law and lead to kufr. The answer will show harmony.

Key Takeaway
The objection forces us to recognize that esoteric meaning must complement, not contradict, the outward law; otherwise, the foundation of Islam is undermined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Apparent and Inner: No Contradiction in Sharia
Ghazali answers a question about whether inner meanings can contradict the apparent, and introduces the five types of secrets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's decisive ruling that the inner meaning (batin) of revelation cannot contradict the apparent (zahir), and how he redirects the question to the higher science of unveiling.

Core Idea
Claiming the inner contradicts the apparent is closer to disbelief than faith.

In this passage, Ghazali addresses a fundamental question about the relationship between the apparent meanings of revelation and their inner secrets. He firmly rejects any notion that the inner could contradict the outward Sharia, as this would undermine the entire religion. He also outlines his methodological approach, distinguishing between the science of transactions (mu'amala) addressed in this book and the higher science of unveiling (mukashafa).

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage once. The objector presents a dilemma: if inner contradicts apparent, Sharia is invalid; if not, there are no secrets. Notice the logical structure.
2
Identify Ghazali's methodological response
Ghazali first says that this question belongs to the science of unveiling (mukashafa), which is beyond the scope of this book on mu'amala. He emphasizes that the creeds here are heart-works, not matters of unveiling.
3
Find the core ruling
Despite the methodological warning, Ghazali gives a clear ruling: whoever claims that inner truth (haqiqa) contradicts the Sharia, or that batin contradicts zahir, is closer to disbelief than to faith.
This is a strong doctrinal statement against antinomianism.
4
Preview the five types of secrets
The passage ends by stating that the secrets of the near ones (muqarrabun) are of five divisions. Though not enumerated here, this sets up the next discussion.
The enumeration appears in the following text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : فإن قلت : هذه الآيات (۳) والأخبار يتطرق إليها تأويلات ، فبين لنا كيفية إختلاف الظاهر والباطن ، فإن الباطن إن كان مناقضا للظاهر ففيه إبطال الشرع ، وهو قول من قال إن الحقيقة خلاف الشريعة ، وهو كفر ، لأن الشريعة عبارة عن الظاهر (٤) ، والحقيقة عبارة عن الباطن (٥) ، وإن كان لا يناقضه ولا يخالفه فهو هو ، فيزول به الإنقسام (۱) ، ولا يكون للشرع سر لا يفشى ، بل يكون الخفي والجلي واحدا فاعلم أن هذا السؤال يحرك خطبا عظيما ، وينجر إلى علوم المكاشفة ويخرج عن مقصود علم المعاملة (٢) ، وهو غرض هذه الكتب ، فإن العقائد التي ذكرناها من أعمال القلوب وقد تعبدنا بتلقينها بالقلوب والتصديق بعقد القلب عليها (۳) ، لا بأن يتوصل إلى أن ينكشف لنا حقائقها ، فإن ذلك لم يكلف به كافة الخلق (٤)، ولولا أنه (٥) الأعمال لما أوردناه في هذا الكتاب ، ولولا أنه عمل ظاهر القلب لا عمل باطنه لما أوردناه في الشطر الأول من الكتاب وإنما الكشف الحقيقي (٦) هو صفة سر القلب وباطنه ، ولكن إذا بحر الكلام إلى تحريك خيال في مناقضة الظاهر للباطن فلا بد من كلام وجيز في حله(٧) فمن قال : إن الحقيقة تخالف الشريعة ، أو الباطن يناقض الظاهر ، فهو إلى الكفر أقرب منه إلى الإيمان ، بل الأسرار التي يختص بها المقربون يدركها ، ولا يشاركهم الأكثرون في عملها ، ويمتنعون عن إفشائها إليهم ترجع إلى خمسة أقسام (۸)
Question: If you say: These verses and reports are subject to interpretations, so explain to us the manner of difference between the apparent and the inner. For if the inner contradicts the apparent, then that entails abrogation of the Sharia, and that is the statement of those who say that reality is contrary to the Sharia, and that is disbelief, because the Sharia is the expression of the apparent, and reality is the expression of the inner. And if it does not contradict it nor oppose it, then it is the same, so the division would cease, and the Sharia would have no secret that is not divulged, but rather the hidden and the manifest would be one. Know that this question stirs great matters, and leads to the sciences of disclosure (mukashafa) and goes beyond the purpose of the science of transactions (mu'amala), which is the goal of these books. For the creeds that we have mentioned are among the works of the hearts, and we have been commanded to instill them in the hearts and to affirm them by tying the heart to them, not by attaining that their realities are disclosed to us; for that is not required of all creation. And were it not that they are works, we would not have mentioned them in this book; and were it not that it is a work of the apparent heart, not a work of its inner, we would not have mentioned them in the first part of the book. Rather, true unveiling is the attribute of the secret of the heart and its inner. But when the discussion moves to stirring an imagination about the contradiction of the apparent and the inner, there is no avoiding a brief statement in its resolution. So whoever says that reality contradicts the Sharia, or that the inner contradicts the apparent, he is closer to disbelief than to faith. Rather, the secrets that the near ones (muqarrabun) are distinguished by - they perceive them, and the majority do not share with them in their action, and they refrain from divulging them to them - reduce to five divisions.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (mas'ala). The objector raises a dilemma: if the inner meaning (batin) of revelation contradicts the apparent (zahir), then the Sharia is invalidated; but if there is no contradiction, then there is no distinction between apparent and inner, and all meaning is public. Ghazali responds by first noting that this question touches on the science of unveiling (mukashafa), which is beyond the scope of this book on the science of transactions (mu'amala). He stresses that the creeds discussed in this work are matters of heart-work (a'mal al-qulub) that are to be affirmed by tying the heart to them, not by exploring their ultimate realities, as that is not required of all people. However, because the question has arisen, he gives a brief resolution: whoever claims that inner truth (haqiqa) contradicts the Sharia, or that batin contradicts zahir, is closer to disbelief than to faith. He then introduces the idea that the secrets of the near ones (muqarrabun) are of five types, which he will enumerate (presumably in the following text). The passage thus combines a methodological warning with a decisive doctrinal ruling, and sets up the upcoming fivefold classification.

باطن
حقيقة

مكاشفة
معاملة

مقربون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The inner meaning (batin) of revelation always contradicts the apparent meaning (zahir).
Correction: Ghazali rules that such a claim is closer to disbelief than to faith; the inner and apparent do not contradict each other.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on someone who claims that the inner (batin) contradicts the apparent (zahir) of Sharia?
A) He is a believer
B) He is closer to disbelief than to faith
C) He is a hypocrite
D) It is permissible

Key Takeaway
Ghazali decisively rejects any contradiction between the inner and apparent meanings of Sharia, as such a view threatens the integrity of the religion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a verse or hadith that seems to challenge your current understanding, do you rush to find a 'deeper meaning' that might let you off the hook, or do you submit to the apparent meaning first? Ghazali warns that claiming contradiction is near kufr. How does that strike you personally? Are you willing to embrace the apparent even when it is difficult?
?
Ghazali says that the creeds are works of the heart that we are commanded to affirm, not necessarily to unveil. Is your faith anchored more in intellectual certainty or in heart-felt surrender? Where in your life have you over-intellectualized a matter of belief instead of simply tying your heart to it?
?
If someone told you that the inner meaning of a hadith makes its outward ruling irrelevant, how would you respond using this lesson? Would you have the courage to say that such a view is closer to disbelief? What would it cost you to defend the harmony of the apparent and inner?

The Harmony of Exoteric and Esoteric: The First Category of Secrets
Ghazali refutes contradiction between sharia and reality, then outlines the first category of secret knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's principle that sharia and reality cannot contradict, and why some truths (like the nature of the soul) must remain hidden from those unable to grasp them.

Core Idea
True secrets protect the weak; they never contradict the law.

This lesson tackles a crucial issue in Islamic theology: how do we reconcile outer religious commands with inner spiritual realities? Imam Ghazali firmly rejects any claim of contradiction. He then begins to explain a classification of esoteric secrets, starting with the most delicate truths — those so subtle that they can mislead the unprepared. The prime example is the reality of the soul, which the Prophet himself refrained from explaining fully.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Read the passage's opening: Ghazali is addressing a question that leads to 'sciences of unveiling'. Note that his main focus here is on 'the science of practice', not unveiling itself.
This sets the boundary of the book's scope.
2
Absorb the refutation of contradiction
Identify Ghazali's strong statement: whoever says reality opposes the Law is near disbelief. This is a key principle: exoteric and esoteric are in harmony.
This refutes a common misconception.
3
Find the five categories
Note that the secrets of the elite reduce to five categories. The passage only explains the first. Skim to see the transition.
The passage is cut off, so we only have one category.
4
Analyze the first category
The first category: truths too subtle for common minds. The elite perceive them but must conceal them. The example is the soul (ruh). Explain why concealment is a mercy, not a deficiency.
The Prophet knew the soul's reality but remained silent by divine command.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this principle applies to other areas of faith: some knowledge is reserved for those prepared to receive it.
This balances the pursuit of knowledge with wisdom in dissemination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاعلم أن هذا السؤال يحرك خطبا عظيما، وينجر إلى علوم المكاشفة ويخرج عن مقصود علم المعاملة، وهو غرض هذه الكتب، فإن العقائد التي ذكرناها من أعمال القلوب وقد تعبدنا بتلقينها بالقلوب والتصديق بعقد القلب عليها، لا بأن يتوصل إلى أن ينكشف لنا حقائقها، فإن ذلك لم يكلف به كافة الخلق، ولولا أنه الأعمال لما أوردناه في هذا الكتاب، ولولا أنه عمل ظاهر القلب لا عمل باطنه لما أوردناه في الشطر الأول من الكتاب. وإنما الكشف الحقيقي هو صفة سر القلب وباطنه، ولكن إذا تحير الكلام إلى تحريك خيال في مناقضة الظاهر للباطن فلا بد من كلام وجيز في حله. فمن قال: إن الحقيقة تخالف الشريعة، أو الباطن يناقض الظاهر، فهو إلى الكفر أقرب منه إلى الإيمان، بل الأسرار التي يختص بها المقربون يدركها، ولا يشاركهم الأكثرون في علمها، ويمتنعون عن إفشائها إليهم ترجع إلى خمسة أقسام. القسم الأول: أن يكون الشيء في نفسه دقيقا تكل أكثر الأفهام عن دركه، فيختص بدركه الخواص، وعليهم أن لا يفشوه إلى غير أهله، فيصير ذلك فتنة عليهم حيث تقصر أفهامهم عن الدرك، وإخفاء سر الروح وكف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيانه من هذا القسم فإن حقيقته مما تكل الأفهام عن دركه، وتقصر الأوهام عن تصور كنهه. ولا تظنن أن ذلك لم يكن مكشوفا لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن من لم يعرف الروح لم يعرف نفسه، ومن لم يعرف نفسه، فكيف يعرف ربه سبحانه؟ ولا يبعد أن يكون ذلك مكشوفا لبعض الأولياء والعلماء، وإن لم يكونوا أنبياء ولكنهم يتأدبون بآداب الشرع فيسكتون عما سكت عنه، بل في صفات الله...
Know that this question stirs great discourse, and leads to the sciences of unveiling and departs from the purpose of the science of practice, which is the aim of these books. Indeed the creeds we have mentioned are works of the hearts, and we have been commanded to instill them in hearts and to affirm them by the contract of the heart, not that we should attain to the unveiling of their realities, for that has not been required of the generality of creation. Were it not that they are deeds, we would not have included them in this book; and were it not that they are work of the outer heart, not work of its inner, we would not have included them in the first part of the book. True unveiling is an attribute of the secret of the heart and its inwardness. But when discourse leads to stirring an imagination that the apparent contradicts the hidden, then brief speech in resolving it is necessary. Whoever says that reality opposes the Law, or that the hidden contradicts the apparent, is closer to disbelief than to faith. Rather, the secrets that the near ones (muqarrabun) are distinguished by, which they perceive, and the majority do not share with them in knowledge of them, and they refrain from disclosing them to [the majority] reduce to five categories. The first category: that a thing is in itself subtle, such that most intellects are too weak to grasp it, so the elite are singled out to perceive it, and they must not disclose it to other than its people, lest it become a trial for them because their intellects fall short of perception. And the concealment of the secret of the soul (ruh) and the restraint of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, from explaining it belong to this category, for its reality is such that intellects are too weak to grasp it, and imaginations fall short of conceiving its quiddity. Do not think that it was not unveiled to the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, for whoever does not know the soul does not know himself, and whoever does not know himself, how can he know his Lord, exalted is He? It is not unlikely that it be unveiled to some saints and scholars, even if they are not prophets, but they are well-mannered with the manners of the Law and remain silent about what He was silent about, indeed regarding the attributes of God...
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a combined refutation and classification. Ghazali begins by addressing a potential objection: how can there be apparent contradictions between the exoteric (zahir) and esoteric (batin) aspects of religion? He strongly warns that claiming such a contradiction is near disbelief. He then asserts that the esoteric secrets known to the elite (muqarrabun) are limited to five categories, and begins to explain the first. The first category comprises truths so subtle that most minds cannot grasp them. The elite, who do understand them, must not disclose them to the unqualified, as this would become a trial for them. The prime example is the true nature of the soul (ruh). The Prophet himself refrained from explaining it, as God says in the Quran: 'Say: The soul is of the command of my Lord, and you have not been given of knowledge except a little.' Ghazali emphasizes that the Prophet did know the reality of the soul, but he was commanded to remain silent. Similarly, saints and scholars who may be granted unveiling must adhere to the Law and remain silent about what the Prophet was silent about. The passage ends abruptly while discussing the attributes of God, indicating that further categories would follow.

أسرار
ظاهر
باطن
كشف
مقربون
خواص
روح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think there is a real contradiction between the exoteric teachings of Islam and esoteric spiritual truths.
Correction: Ghazali asserts that claiming such a contradiction is near disbelief; the two are in harmony. Apparent conflicts arise from limitations in understanding.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ghazali, why did the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) remain silent about the reality of the soul?
A) He did not know it.
B) It is too subtle for most minds to grasp and would cause trial.
C) It was unknown to the angels.
D) It was not important for faith.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali establishes that sharia and reality are in harmony, and that some truths, like the essence of the soul, are hidden not because they are false but because they are too profound for common understanding.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your inner spiritual experiences or insights conflicted with an external ruling of the Sharia? How did you resolve that tension, and what does Ghazali's strong warning tell you about the correct stance?
?
You claim to know yourself, but do you truly know the reality of your own soul? If the Prophet himself knew it and you don't, are you content with that ignorance, or will you seek the path of kashf through purification and following the sunnah?
?
The elite must conceal profound truths to protect others from trial. Are you guilty of sharing deep spiritual insights with those who are not ready, or do you impatiently demand such knowledge before you have prepared your heart? What step will you take today to correct this?

The Principle of Concealing Subtle Knowledge
Ghazali introduces the first division of knowledge and the soul example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why certain subtle truths, like the reality of the soul, are withheld from the general public and reserved for the elite.

Core Idea
Subtle truths are dangerous for the masses; the wise keep them hidden.

Imam Ghazali begins by distinguishing between two types of knowledge: what can be shared broadly and what must be kept among the elite. The soul's reality is a prime example—so delicate that even the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not disclose its essence. This lesson explores the rationale behind such concealment and its importance for safeguarding faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of knowledge
Read the passage and note how Ghazali divides knowledge: one type is subtle and belongs only to the elite (al-khawass). The masses cannot grasp it without harm.
Look for the phrase 'يختص بدركه الخواص'.
2
Understand the soul as an example
Ghazali uses the secret of the soul (sirr al-ruh) as a case. Notice why the Prophet (s) refrained from explaining it—not because he didn't know, but because it's beyond common understanding.
The Prophet’s knowledge is affirmed; his silence is wisdom, not ignorance.
3
Reflect on the role of saints and scholars
Even those who grasp such truths follow the Prophet’s example and remain silent. Why? To prevent confusion and trial.
This shows the responsibility of the learned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول - أن يكون الشيء في نفسه دقيقاً تكل أكثر الأفهام عن دركه ، فيختص بدركه الخواص (۱) ، وعليهم أن لا يفشوه إلى غير أهله (۲) ، فيصير ذلك فتنة عليهم حيث تقصر أفهامهم عن الدرك ، وإخفاء سر الروح وكف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيانه » من هذا القـ القسم (۳) فإن حقيقته مما تكل الأفهام عن دركه ، وتقصر الأوهام عن تصور كنهه(٤). ولا تظنن أن ذلك لم يكن مكشوفا لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فإن من لم يعرف الروح لم يعرف نفسه ، ومن لم يعرف نفسه ، فكيف يعرف ربه سبحانه(٥) ؟ ولا يبعد أن يكون ذلك مكشوفاً لبعض الأولياء والعلماء(٦) ، وإن لم يكونوا أنبياء ولكنهم يتأدبون بآداب الشرع فيسكتون عما سكت عنه (۷) ، بل في صفات الله عز وجل من الخفايا ما تقصر أفهام الجماهير عن دركه ، ولم يذكر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم منها إلا الظواهر للأفهام : من العلم ، والقدرة ، وغيرهما ، حتى فهمها الخلق بنوع مناسبة توهموها إلى علمهم وقدرتهم إذ كان لهم من الأوصاف ما يسمى علما وقدرة، فيتوهمون ذلك بنوع مقايسة ، ولو ذكر من صفاته ، ما ليس للخلق مما يناسبه بعض المناسبة شيء لم يفهموه (۱) ، بل لذة الجماع إذا ذكرت للصبي أو العنين (٢) لم يفهمها إلا بمناسبة إلى لذة المطعوم الذي يدركه ، ولا يكون ذلك فهما على التحقيق (۳) ، والمخالفة بين علم الله تعالى وقدرته وعلم الخلق وقدرتهم أكثر المخالفة من بين لذة الجماع والاكل (٤). وللإمام الغزالي في كتابه المقصد الأسني كلام نفيس قال فيه : وإنما غاية هذا الوصف إيهام وتشبيه ومشاركة في الإسم لكن يقطع التشبيه بأن يقال : ليس كمثله شيء ، فهو حي كالإحياء ، وقادر لا كالقادرين ؛ كما يقال الوقاع لذيذ كالسكر ولكن تلك اللذة لا تشبه هذه البتة ، ولكن تشاركها في الإسم، وكان إذا عرفنا أن الله تعالى حي عالم قدير ، فلم نعرف أولا إلا بأنفسنا إذ الأصم لا يتصور أن يفهم معنى قولنا : إن الله سميع ، ولا الاكمه معنى قولنا إن الله بصير، وكذلك إذا قال القائل كيف يكون الله عالما بالأشياء؟ فنقول له : كما تعلم أنت أشياء فلا يمكنه أن يفهم شيئا إلا إذا كان فيه ما يناسبه فيعلم أولاً ما هو منصف به ، ثم يعلم غيره بالمناسبة إليه ، فإذا كان الله تعالى وصفه وخاصية ليس فينا ما يناسبه ويشاركه ولو في الإسم لم يتصور فهمه البتة ، فما عرف أحد إلا نفسه ، ثم قايس بين صفات الله تعالى وبين صفات نفسه ، وتتعالى صفات الله وتتقدس عن أن تشبه صفاتنا » اهـ
The first division: That a thing is in itself subtle, such that most intellects tire from comprehending it, so it is grasped only by the elite (1), and they must not disclose it to those not worthy of it (2), lest it become a trial for them because their intellects fall short of comprehension. And the concealment of the secret of the soul and the Prophet's (peace be upon him) refraining from explaining it is from this division (3), for its reality is among those things at which intellects tire from grasping and imaginations fall short of conceiving its essence (4). And do not think that this was not disclosed to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), for whoever does not know the soul does not know himself, and whoever does not know himself, how can he know his Lord, glorified is He (5)? And it is not far-fetched that this is disclosed to some saints and scholars (6), even if they are not prophets, but they observe the etiquette of the Law and remain silent about that concerning which he remained silent (7). Rather, among the attributes of Allah Almighty there are hidden matters at which the understandings of the masses fall short, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) only mentioned from them the apparent ones for the understandings: such as knowledge, power, and others, so that the creation understood them by a kind of similarity they imagined to their own knowledge and power, since they have attributes called knowledge and power, so they imagined that by a kind of comparison. Had he mentioned from His attributes something of which the creation has nothing that resembles it even partially, they would not have understood it (1). Rather, the pleasure of intercourse if mentioned to a boy or an impotent man (2) is not understood except by analogy to the pleasure of food that he perceives, and that is not true comprehension (3). And the difference between Allah's knowledge and power and the knowledge and power of the creation is greater than the difference between the pleasure of intercourse and eating (4). And Imam Ghazali in his book al-Maqsad al-Asna has valuable words in which he said: 'The utmost of this description is only suggestion, comparison, and sharing in the name, but comparison is cut off by saying: “Nothing is like Him.” So He is living not like the living, powerful not like the powerful; just as it is said: coitus is delicious like sugar, but that pleasure does not resemble this at all, but they share in the name. And if we know that Allah is living, knowing, powerful, we did not know that except first through ourselves, for the deaf cannot conceive understanding the meaning of our saying: Allah is Hearing, nor the blind the meaning of our saying: Allah is Seeing. Similarly, if someone says: How is Allah knowing of things? We say to him: As you know things. So he cannot understand anything unless there is in it something that resembles it, so he first knows what he is described with, then knows other things by analogy to it. If Allah's description and property are such that there is nothing in us that resembles it and shares it even in name, it cannot be conceived at all. So no one knows except himself, then compares between Allah's attributes and his own attributes, and exalted and holy are Allah's attributes from resembling our attributes.' End quote.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument by Imam Ghazali about the principle of concealing certain subtle knowledge from the general public. He begins by classifying one type of knowledge: matters that are inherently too subtle for most intellects to grasp. These are to be kept only among the elite (الخواص), who must not disclose them to those unworthy (غير أهله), as it would cause confusion and trial. He gives the example of the secret of the soul (سر الروح) and the Prophet's (saw) silence about its essence, as reported in hadith. Ghazali emphasizes that the Prophet did know the reality of the soul (otherwise he would not know himself nor his Lord), but he refrained from explaining it because it is beyond common comprehension. He adds that some saints and deep scholars may also know it, but they follow the Prophet's example and remain silent. Ghazali then extends this to divine attributes: the Prophet only mentioned those attributes that humans can partially understand by analogy, like knowledge and power, because humans have some share in these names. If he had mentioned attributes that have no analogy in human experience, people would not understand and might even reject them. He illustrates with the analogy of a boy or an impotent man trying to understand sexual pleasure by comparing it to the pleasure of food—this analogy is insufficient and not true comprehension. The difference between God's attributes and human attributes is far greater than between different kinds of pleasure. Finally, Ghazali quotes his own work al-Maqsad al-Asna to clarify that any description of God is only suggestive and shares names, but the reality is utterly different. He explains that we first know attributes from ourselves, then attribute them to God by analogy, but we must affirm that there is nothing like Him. This guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih) while affirming the attributes.

Key Terms
الخواص
الجماهير
الروح
سر الروح
الأولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet (s) did not know the reality of the soul because he did not explain it.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly states that the Prophet did know it, as knowing the soul is necessary for knowing oneself and Allah, but he concealed it because it is beyond the grasp of most intellects.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why did the Prophet (s) refrain from explaining the reality of the soul?
A) Because he did not know it himself.
B) Because its reality is too subtle for most intellects and would cause confusion.
C) Because he was ordered never to speak about it.
D) Because the soul is not important to know.

Key Takeaway
Subtle truths like the reality of the soul are concealed from the masses to protect them, and the wise follow the Prophet's example of silence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ghazali says subtle truths can become a trial for those not ready. Think of a time you shared a religious insight with someone who was not prepared. Did it help or harm them? Will you be more cautious in the future?
?
The Prophet knew the reality of the soul but remained silent. Is there a truth about yourself or your faith that you know but choose not to disclose because it would not benefit others? What is it, and are you willing to keep it hidden for their sake?
?
You are pursuing knowledge. Are you doing so to become part of the elite who can handle subtle truths, or are you seeking to gain status? How will you ensure your knowledge leads to humility and silence when needed, not pride and careless speech?

Understanding Divine Attributes Without Comparison
Ghazali extends the concealment principle to divine attributes and clarifies the role of analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's attributes cannot be fully grasped by analogy with human attributes, and how shared names do not imply resemblance.

Core Idea
God's attributes are utterly unique; shared names hide infinite difference.

Building on the principle of concealment, Ghazali now turns to divine attributes. The Prophet only mentioned attributes like knowledge and power because humans have some share in those names, but the reality is incomparably different. Using the analogy of pleasure, Ghazali shows how our understanding is limited, and he quotes his own work to emphasize that any description is mere suggestion, not true likeness.

Guided Path
1
Note the limits of prophetic disclosure on attributes
Read how Ghazali says the Prophet only revealed apparent attributes that humans can partially grasp by similarity. If something had no analogy, it would not be understood.
Look for 'ولو ذكر من صفاته ما ليس للخلق...'
2
Analyze the analogy of pleasure
Ghazali compares understanding divine attributes to a boy trying to understand sexual pleasure by comparing it to food. Understand the point: such analogies fall short.
The difference between God and creatures is greater than between two pleasures.
3
Learn from the quote from al-Maqsad al-Asna
Ghazali explains that we only know attributes through ourselves first, but we must cut off resemblance by affirming 'Nothing is like Him.' Shared names do not mean shared reality.
The deaf cannot understand hearing; the blind cannot understand sight.

أو العنين (٢) لم يفهمها إلا بمناسبة إلى لذة المطعوم الذي يدركه ، ولا يكون ذلك فهما على التحقيق (۳) ، والمخالفة بين علم الله تعالى وقدرته وعلم الخلق وقدرتهم أكثر المخالفة من بين لذة الجماع والاكل (٤). وللإمام الغزالي في كتابه المقصد الأسني كلام نفيس قال فيه : وإنما غاية هذا الوصف إيهام وتشبيه ومشاركة في الإسم لكن يقطع التشبيه بأن يقال : ليس كمثله شيء ، فهو حي كالإحياء ، وقادر لا كالقادرين ؛ كما يقال الوقاع لذيذ كالسكر ولكن تلك اللذة لا تشبه هذه البتة ، ولكن تشاركها في الإسم، وكان إذا عرفنا أن الله تعالى حي عالم قدير ، فلم نعرف أولا إلا بأنفسنا إذ الأصم لا يتصور أن يفهم معنى قولنا : إن الله سميع ، ولا الاكمه معنى قولنا إن الله بصير، وكذلك إذا قال القائل كيف يكون الله عالما بالأشياء؟ فنقول له : كما تعلم أنت أشياء فلا يمكنه أن يفهم شيئا إلا إذا كان فيه ما يناسبه فيعلم أولاً ما هو منصف به ، ثم يعلم غيره بالمناسبة إليه ، فإذا كان الله تعالى وصفه وخاصية ليس فينا ما يناسبه ويشاركه ولو في الإسم لم يتصور فهمه البتة ، فما عرف أحد إلا نفسه ، ثم قايس بين صفات الله تعالى وبين صفات نفسه ، وتتعالى صفات الله وتتقدس عن أن تشبه صفاتنا » اهـ
The first division: That a thing is in itself subtle, such that most intellects tire from comprehending it, so it is grasped only by the elite (1), and they must not disclose it to those not worthy of it (2), lest it become a trial for them because their intellects fall short of comprehension. And the concealment of the secret of the soul and the Prophet's (peace be upon him) refraining from explaining it is from this division (3), for its reality is among those things at which intellects tire from grasping and imaginations fall short of conceiving its essence (4). And do not think that this was not disclosed to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), for whoever does not know the soul does not know himself, and whoever does not know himself, how can he know his Lord, glorified is He (5)? And it is not far-fetched that this is disclosed to some saints and scholars (6), even if they are not prophets, but they observe the etiquette of the Law and remain silent about that concerning which he remained silent (7). Rather, among the attributes of Allah Almighty there are hidden matters at which the understandings of the masses fall short, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) only mentioned from them the apparent ones for the understandings: such as knowledge, power, and others, so that the creation understood them by a kind of similarity they imagined to their own knowledge and power, since they have attributes called knowledge and power, so they imagined that by a kind of comparison. Had he mentioned from His attributes something of which the creation has nothing that resembles it even partially, they would not have understood it (1). Rather, the pleasure of intercourse if mentioned to a boy or an impotent man (2) is not understood except by analogy to the pleasure of food that he perceives, and that is not true comprehension (3). And the difference between Allah's knowledge and power and the knowledge and power of the creation is greater than the difference between the pleasure of intercourse and eating (4). And Imam Ghazali in his book al-Maqsad al-Asna has valuable words in which he said: 'The utmost of this description is only suggestion, comparison, and sharing in the name, but comparison is cut off by saying: “Nothing is like Him.” So He is living not like the living, powerful not like the powerful; just as it is said: coitus is delicious like sugar, but that pleasure does not resemble this at all, but they share in the name. And if we know that Allah is living, knowing, powerful, we did not know that except first through ourselves, for the deaf cannot conceive understanding the meaning of our saying: Allah is Hearing, nor the blind the meaning of our saying: Allah is Seeing. Similarly, if someone says: How is Allah knowing of things? We say to him: As you know things. So he cannot understand anything unless there is in it something that resembles it, so he first knows what he is described with, then knows other things by analogy to it. If Allah's description and property are such that there is nothing in us that resembles it and shares it even in name, it cannot be conceived at all. So no one knows except himself, then compares between Allah's attributes and his own attributes, and exalted and holy are Allah's attributes from resembling our attributes.' End quote.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument by Imam Ghazali about the principle of concealing certain subtle knowledge from the general public. He begins by classifying one type of knowledge: matters that are inherently too subtle for most intellects to grasp. These are to be kept only among the elite (الخواص), who must not disclose them to those unworthy (غير أهله), as it would cause confusion and trial. He gives the example of the secret of the soul (سر الروح) and the Prophet's (saw) silence about its essence, as reported in hadith. Ghazali emphasizes that the Prophet did know the reality of the soul (otherwise he would not know himself nor his Lord), but he refrained from explaining it because it is beyond common comprehension. He adds that some saints and deep scholars may also know it, but they follow the Prophet's example and remain silent. Ghazali then extends this to divine attributes: the Prophet only mentioned those attributes that humans can partially understand by analogy, like knowledge and power, because humans have some share in these names. If he had mentioned attributes that have no analogy in human experience, people would not understand and might even reject them. He illustrates with the analogy of a boy or an impotent man trying to understand sexual pleasure by comparing it to the pleasure of food—this analogy is insufficient and not true comprehension. The difference between God's attributes and human attributes is far greater than between different kinds of pleasure. Finally, Ghazali quotes his own work al-Maqsad al-Asna to clarify that any description of God is only suggestive and shares names, but the reality is utterly different. He explains that we first know attributes from ourselves, then attribute them to God by analogy, but we must affirm that there is nothing like Him. This guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih) while affirming the attributes.

Key Terms
التشبيه
المقايسة
المشاركة في الاسم
الظواهر
الخواص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: When we say God is 'knowing' or 'powerful,' we mean exactly what we mean when we say a human is knowing or powerful.
Correction: Ghazali argues that these names are shared, but the realities are utterly different. The difference is greater than between the pleasure of intercourse and eating.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why did the Prophet only mention attributes like knowledge and power?
A) Because those are the only attributes God has.
B) Because humans have some share in those names and can partially grasp them by analogy.
C) Because the Prophet did not know the other attributes.
D) Because the other attributes are not important.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are unique and beyond full human comprehension; shared names require us to affirm them while denying any resemblance to creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Allah is All-Knowing,' do you ever stop to realize that His knowledge is not like yours—even at its best? How does that truth challenge the way you approach your own limited understanding of His plans? This week, before making a decision, pause and say: 'My knowledge is partial, but His is completely other.' Then act with trust.
?
If the Prophet himself did not reveal all of God's attributes because you couldn't grasp them, what does that say about your intellectual pride when you try to 'figure out' God? Will you commit to studying His names with humility, stopping where the revelation stops, rather than speculating?
?
Imagine you have been describing God's power as 'just like a human's but bigger.' After reading this passage, you realize the difference is greater than between two completely different pleasures. How does that change the way you think about His power in your life? Will you now, when you say 'Allah is Powerful,' actively remind yourself that it is not like any power you know?

The Second Category of Hidden Truths: Wisdom in Concealment
Ghazali defines the second category of hidden truths and illustrates with qadar, veils, and the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's concept of the second category of hidden truths and why certain truths like the secret of qadar and the veils are concealed despite being intellectually understandable.

Core Idea
Some truths are too powerful for fragile minds; concealment is mercy, not obscurantism.

Ghazali continues his classification of hidden truths. After the first category of things beyond intellect, he now discusses truths that are understandable but harmful to disclose. This lesson explores the wisdom behind concealing such truths, using the secret of qadar and the veils of Allah as examples. You will see how Ghazali defends the divine concealment as a form of protection for the listener.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let Ghazali's argument unfold naturally.
Notice how he defines the second category right at the beginning.
2
Examine the analogies
Ghazali uses analogies of sunlight harming bats and rose scent harming dung beetles. Ask yourself: what do these analogies teach about the listener's capacity?
The harm is relative to the recipient, not the truth itself.
3
Identify the examples: qadar, veils, and the Hour
Three concrete examples are given: the secret of qadar (divine decree), the hadiths about veils of light, and the concealment of the Hour's time. For each, note why disclosure would be harmful.
The qadar example is further explained with the risk of suggesting foolishness or injustice.
4
Understand the veil interpretation
Abu Mansur al-Tamimi explains that the veils are on the creation, not on Allah. Read the Quranic proof (83:15) and see how it supports this.
This refutes any anthropomorphism about Allah being 'behind' a veil.
5
Reflect on the practical wisdom
The Hour's timing is hidden because knowing it might lead to complacency if long, or despair if short. Connect this to the overall theme: mercy in concealment.
Concealment is not due to irrationality but due to divine wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثاني - من الخفيات التي تمتنع الأنبياء والصديقون عن ذكرها ما هو مفهوم في نفسه لا يكل الفهم عنه ، ولكن ذكره يضر بأكثر المستمعين ، ولا يضر بالأنبياء والصديقين وسر القدر الذي منع أهل العلم من إفشائه من هذا القسم ، فلا يبعد أن يكون ذكر بعض الحقائق مضراً ببعض الخلق ، كما يضر نور الشمس بأبصار الخفافيش وكما تضر رياح الورد بالجعل ، وكيف يبعد هذا وقولنا أن الكفر والزنا والمعاصي والشرور كله بقضاء الله تعالى وارادته ومشيئته حق في نفسه وقد أضر حديث أنس رضي الله عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لجبريل: هل ترى ربك؟ قال: إن بيني وبينه لسبعين حجاباً من نور. وفي المعجم الكبير للإمام الطبراني من حديث سهل بن سعد: دون الله تعالى سبعون ألف حجاب من نور وظلمة. وفي مسلم من حديث أبي موسى: حجابه من النور لو كشفه لأحرقت سبحات وجهه ما انتهى إليه بصره من خلقه. ولابن ماجه: كل شيء أدركه بصره. ولأبي منصور التميمي كلام نفيس جداً قال فيه: كل خبر ذكر فيه الحجاب فإنه يرجع معناه إلى الخلق لأنهم هم المحجوبون عن رؤية الله عز وجل، وليس الخالق محجوباً عنهم فساتره أكبر منه، وليس الله عز وجل حدّ ولا نهاية فلا أن يكون بغيره مستوراً. يصح ودليله قوله عز وجل: ﴿ كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ عَنْ رَّبِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ لَمَحْجُوبُونَ ﴾، ولم يقل إنه محجوب عنهم. ويراهم ولا يجوز أن يكون مستوراً بحجاب لأن ما ستره عن غيره سماعه بقوم، إذ أوهم ذلك عندهم أنه دلالة على السفه، ونقيض الحكمة والرضا بالقبيح والظلم. وكذلك سر القدر ولو أفشى لأوهم عند أكثر الخلق عجزا إذا تقصر أفهامهم عن إدراك ما يزيل ذلك الوهم عنهم ولو قال قائل: إن القيامة لو ذكر ميقاتها وأنها بعد ألف سنة أو أكثر أو أقل لكان مفهوماً، ولكن لم يذكر لمصلحة العباد وخوفا من الضرر، فلعل المدة إليها بعيدة فيطول الأمد، وإذا استبطأت النفوس وقت العقاب قل إكتراثها، ولعلها
The second category – of the hidden things that the prophets and the truthful ones refrain from mentioning is that which is understood in itself, the intellect is not incapable of grasping it, but its mention harms most listeners, and it does not harm the prophets and the truthful ones. And the secret of al-qadar (divine decree) which the people of knowledge were forbidden to disclose is of this category. So it is not far-fetched that the mention of some truths may be harmful to some creatures, just as the light of the sun harms the eyesight of bats, and just as the scent of roses harms the dung beetle. And how far-fetched can this be when we say that kufr (disbelief), zina (adultery), sins, and evils – all of it – are by the decree of Allah, Most High, His will, and His volition, true in itself, and hearing it has harmed some people, since it suggested to them that it indicates foolishness, the opposite of wisdom, and satisfaction with evil and injustice. And likewise, the secret of qadar – if it had been disclosed, it would have suggested to most people an inability, when their minds fall short of grasping what removes that illusion from them. And if someone were to say: 'If the time of the Hour (the Day of Judgment) were mentioned – that it would be after a thousand years or more or less – it would have been understood, but it was not mentioned for the benefit of the servants and out of fear of harm. Perhaps the period to it is long, so the time seems extended, and when souls become impatient regarding the time of punishment, their concern diminishes, and perhaps...'
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argumentative explanation. Ghazali first defines the second category of hidden truths: those that are intellectually understandable but whose disclosure harms listeners, while not harming the prophets and the truthful. He then gives the secret of qadar as an example. He argues that it is not far-fetched that some truths are harmful to mention, using analogies: sunlight harms bats, rose scent harms dung beetles. He extends this to stating that all disbelief, adultery, sins, and evils are by Allah's decree – though true in itself, hearing it has harmed some people by suggesting foolishness and injustice. This is followed by a hadith section about the veils of Allah (hijab). Ghazali cites multiple hadith narrations about the veils of light and then presents the interpretation of Abu Mansur al-Tamimi: every report about a veil refers to the creation being veiled from seeing Allah, not Allah being veiled from them, since Allah has no limit or end. The proof is the Quranic verse 'Nay, on that Day they are veiled from their Lord' (83:15), which says they are veiled, not that He is veiled. After the hadith commentary, Ghazali returns to the qadar example, noting that if the secret of qadar were disclosed, it would cause misunderstanding due to limited intellect. Finally, he gives another example: the concealment of the Hour's time – if known, it might be too distant, causing lack of concern. Thus, the passage demonstrates the principle that some truths are hidden for practical benefit.

القدر
الحجاب
الوهم
القضاء
المشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the secret of qadar is inherently irrational or contradictory.
Correction: Ghazali clarifies it is understood but harmful to disclose because of listener limitations.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why does the second category of hidden truths exist?
A) Because they are impossible for anyone to understand.
B) Because their mention would harm most listeners despite being understandable.
C) Because only prophets can understand them.
D) Because they contradict reason.

Key Takeaway
The second category of hidden truths are those that are rationally understandable but whose disclosure would harm most listeners, thus concealment is an act of divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a truth about yourself that you have hidden because revealing it might harm others' perception of you or cause them to stumble. Does this lesson justify your concealment, or is it an excuse for fear? What would it take for you to disclose it with wisdom?
?
The lesson says the secret of qadar is harmful to foolish minds. When you discuss theological matters, do you consider the listener's capacity, or do you speak to show off knowledge? How can you practice gentleness and restraint in your next conversation about predestination?
?
You claim to trust God's wisdom, yet do you secretly wish He had told us the exact time of the Hour so you could plan your life? If you are honest, what does that reveal about your heart's attachment to this world? How will you realign today with the humility of not knowing?

The Wisdom of Concealing the Day of Judgment
Ghazali presents a hypothetical objection and answer about concealing the Day of Judgment's time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the time of the Day of Judgment was concealed, according to Ghazali's argument from divine wisdom.

Core Idea
Concealment of the Day of Judgment is an act of mercy, not arbitrariness.

In this passage, Ghazali addresses a potential objection: why didn't Allah reveal the exact time of the Day of Judgment? He provides a profound answer rooted in divine care for humanity's welfare. Through two scenarios, he shows that revealing the time would either lead to complacency or overwhelming fear, both harmful. Therefore, concealment is a mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get its flow. Then read the translation to grasp the full argument. Notice how Ghazali structures the objection and answer.
The passage uses a conditional structure: 'if it were mentioned... then either... or...'
2
Identify the two scenarios
The answer considers two possibilities: if the time is far off and if it is near. Understand how each leads to a harmful outcome if the time were known.
Far: complacency and diminished concern. Near: excessive fear and abandonment of worldly duties.
3
Reflect on the divine wisdom
Ask yourself: How does this argument demonstrate that concealment is for the benefit of humanity? This connects to the broader theme of divine wisdom in not revealing certain matters.
This passage is an example of the 'category of concealment due to potential harm' mentioned earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال قائل: إن القيامة لو ذكر ميقاتها وأنها بعد ألف سنة أو أكثر أو أقل لكان مفهوما، ولكن لم يذكر لمصلحة العباد وخوفا من الضرر، فلعل المدة إليها بعيدة فيطول الأمد، وإذا استبطأت النفوس وقت العقاب قل إكتراثها، ولعلها كانت قريبة في علم الله سبحانه، ولو ذكرت لعظم الخوف وأعرض الناس عن الأعمال وخربت الدنيا؛ فهذا المعنى لو اتجه وصح فيكون مثالا لهذا القسم.
And if someone said: The Day of Judgment, if its time were mentioned and that it is after a thousand years or more or less, it would be understood, but it was not mentioned for the benefit of the servants and out of fear of harm, for perhaps the period to it is far and the term would be long, and when souls become impatient at the time of punishment their concern diminishes, and perhaps it was near in the knowledge of God, exalted is He, and if it were mentioned the fear would be great and people would turn away from deeds and the world would be ruined; so this meaning, if it is applicable and sound, would be an example for this category.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage presents a hypothetical objection and its answer, serving as an example for the second category (concealment due to potential harm). The objection states that if the exact time of the Day of Judgment were revealed, people would understand it, but it was hidden for the benefit of the servants and to avoid harm. The answer provides two possibilities: if the time is far, people would become complacent and care less about punishment; if the time is near, the fear would be overwhelming, causing people to abandon worldly works and leading to the ruin of the world. Thus, concealing the time safeguards both scenarios, providing a clear example of why some truths are hidden for the greater good.

Key Terms

ميقاتها
مصلحة العباد
خوف الضرر
الأمد
إكتراث
خربت الدنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think concealing the time indicates ignorance or arbitrariness on God's part.
Correction: This passage shows that concealment is an act of divine wisdom and mercy, carefully considering human welfare in both scenarios of time being far or near.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why was the exact time of the Day of Judgment not mentioned?
A) Because it is impossible to know.
B) Because it would cause either complacency or excessive fear, harming people.
C) Because God is unwilling to reveal it.
D) Because the time changes constantly.

Key Takeaway
Concealing the exact time of the Day of Judgment is a divine mercy that prevents human harm from either complacency or overwhelming fear.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself demanding certainty from Allah about the future, impatient with unanswered questions? How does this passage expose the hidden pride in your need to know? Will you today entrust an unknown future to His concealed wisdom?
?
Imagine the Day of Judgment were announced to be exactly one week away. Would your fear lead you to abandon your duties, or would it inspire productive repentance? The passage warns that both extremes—complacency and panic—are harmful. Which tendency do you recognize in yourself, and what step will you take to balance hope and fear?
?
The concealment of the Day of Judgment is described as a mercy. Reflect on a time when Allah hid the outcome of a situation from you. Was that concealment actually a protection? How can you cultivate trust (tawakkul) in Allah's hidden plans, especially when you crave clarity?

Concealment through Metaphor and Allusion (The Third Category)
Ghazali defines the third category of concealment using metaphor for greater impact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's third category of concealment, where metaphor and allusion are used to intensify the impact of a statement on the listener's heart.

Core Idea
Metaphor deepens understanding by engaging the heart, not just the mind.

In this passage, Ghazali introduces a subtle form of concealment: using metaphor and symbol even when explicit speech would be harmless. He explains that this technique magnifies the effect on the listener and reveals deeper meanings to those who reflect. The example of placing pearls on pigs illustrates how the same words can be understood differently by the casual listener and the discerning investigator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the flow from definition to example to poetry.
2
Identify the purpose of metaphor
Ghazali states that metaphor is used to increase the impact on the listener's heart ('ليكون وقعه في قلب المستمع أغلب'). This is not to hide harm but to magnify significance.
Contrast this with the first two categories of concealment.
3
Analyze the example and poem
Unpack the metaphor of pearls and pigs: pearls represent knowledge, pigs unfit recipients. The poem shows how different people interpret the same image—tailor vs weaver—highlighting varying levels of understanding.
Consider how the discerning investigator ('المحقق') moves beyond literal meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث - أن يكون الشيء بحيث لو ذكر صريحاً لفهم ولم يكن فيه ضرر ولكن يكنى عنه على سبيل الإستعارة والرمز، ليكون وقعه في قلب المستمع أغلب، وله مصلحة في أن يعظم وقع ذلك الأمر في قلبه، كما لو قال قائل: رأيت فلانا يقلد الدر في أعناق الخنازير، فكنى به عن إفشاء العلم وبث الحكمة إلى غير أهلها، فالمستمع قد يسبق إلى فهمه ظاهر اللفظ، والمحقق إذا نظر وعلم أن ذلك الإنسان لم يكن معه در، ولا كان في موضعه خنزير، تفطن لدرك السر والباطن، فيتفاوت الناس في ذلك ومن هذا قال الشاعر: رجلان خياط وآخر حائك متقابلان على السماك الأعزل لا زال ينسج ذاك خرقة مدبر ويخيط صاحبه ثياب المقبل
The third category: that a thing is such that if it were mentioned explicitly it would be understood and there would be no harm in it, but it is alluded to by way of metaphor and symbol, so that its impact on the heart of the listener is greater, and there is a benefit in magnifying the impact of that matter in his heart. As if someone said: I saw so-and-so placing pearls around the necks of pigs, thereby alluding to the dissemination of knowledge and the spreading of wisdom to those who are not its people. So the listener may initially understand the literal apparent meaning, but the investigator, when he ponders and knows that that person had no pearls with him, nor was there a pig in that place, becomes attentive to grasping the secret and the inner meaning. Thus people differ in that. And from this the poet said: Two men, a tailor and a weaver, facing each other under the starless sky; the one keeps sewing a patched garment, and the other stitches clothes for the one who advances.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of concealment: when a statement could be made explicitly without harm, but is instead expressed through metaphor and allusion to create a stronger impression on the listener's heart. The example is someone saying 'I saw so-and-so placing pearls around the necks of pigs.' This is a metaphor for giving knowledge and wisdom to those unfit for it. The casual listener hears only the surface meaning, but the discerning person realizes that pearls (knowledge) are not placed on pigs (ignorant people), so he looks for the deeper meaning. This reveals the inner truth more powerfully. The poem that follows illustrates how people can have different interpretations—the tailor and weaver represent contrasting perspectives, and the metaphorical imagery conveys the idea that people's understanding varies. The overall lesson is that figurative language can enhance comprehension and impact, and that true understanding requires insight.

Key Terms
القسم الثالث
الكناية

Allusion for Greater Impact
Ghazali defines the third division of metaphorical expression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's third division of metaphorical expression, where a statement is alluded to metaphorically to increase its impact on the listener, even though literal expression would be harmless.

Core Idea
Metaphor amplifies impact by engaging the listener's reflection.

Imam Ghazali now presents a third category of expression in religious texts: one where the literal meaning is harmless but metaphorical allusion is used to deepen the listener's engagement. He illustrates this with vivid examples, showing how the surface absurdity prompts the thoughtful listener to seek the inner meaning. This lesson unpacks that third division and its pedagogical purpose.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's definition
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key features: the thing is harmless if stated explicitly, yet it is expressed through metaphor and symbolism.
Look for the phrase 'ليكون وقعه في قلب المستمع أغلب' — this is the core purpose.
2
Analyze the example
Examine the example of 'pearls on pigs'. How does the literal absurdity guide the investigator to the intended meaning? Reflect on why Ghazali chose this example.
The investigator uses context to reject the literal meaning and discover the metaphorical one.
3
Consider the poetic illustration
Read the couplet about the tailor and weaver. How does this poetic image convey a celestial cause of approach and withdrawal? Why does Ghazali include a poetic example?
Poetic examples demonstrate that this metaphorical method is not limited to religious texts but is a broader linguistic tool.
4
Summarize the type
Reread Ghazali's concluding sentence: 'expressing the meaning through an image that includes the very meaning or its like.' Formulate in your own words what makes this third division distinct.
Compare this to the previous two divisions (if known) for context, but focus only on this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث - أن يكون الشيء بحيث لو ذكر صريحاً لفهم ولم يكن فيه ضرر ولكن يكنى عنه على سبيل الإستعارة والرمز، ليكون وقعه في قلب المستمع أغلب، وله مصلحة في أن يعظم وقع ذلك الأمر في قلبه، كما لو قال قائل : رأيت فلانا يقلد الدر في أعناق الخنازير، فكنى به عن إفشاء العلم وبث الحكمة إلى غير أهلها، فالمستمع قد يسبق إلى فهمه ظاهر اللفظ، والمحقق إذا نظر وعلم أن ذلك الإنسان لم يكن معه در، ولا كان في موضعه خنزير، تفطن لدرك السر والباطن، فيتفاوت الناس في ذلك ومن هذا قال الشاعر : رجلان خياط وآخر حائك متقابلان على السماك الأعزل لا زال ينسج ذاك خرقة مدبر ويخيط صاحبه ثياب المقبل فإنه عبر عن سبب سماوي في الإقبال والإدبار برجلين صانعين؛ وهذا النوع يرجع إلى التعبير عن المعنى بالصورة التي تتضمن عين المعنى أو مثله،
The third division: that a thing is such that if mentioned explicitly, it would be understood and there is no harm in it, but it is alluded to by way of metaphor and symbolism, so that its impact on the listener's heart is greater, and there is a benefit in magnifying the impact of that matter in his heart. As if someone says: 'I saw so-and-so hanging pearls around the necks of pigs,' alluding thereby to the dissemination of knowledge and the spreading of wisdom to those who are not its people. The listener may first understand the apparent meaning of the utterance, but the investigator, when he reflects and knows that that person did not have pearls with him, nor was there a pig in that place, discerns the secret and the inner meaning. Thus people vary in this. And from this, the poet said: 'Two men, a tailor and another a weaver, facing each other upon the naked Sky Bearer (Simāk al-A‘zal). The one keeps weaving a worn-out garment, and the other sews the clothes of the one who approaches.' For he expressed a celestial cause of approach and withdrawal through two craftsmen. And this type goes back to expressing the meaning through an image that includes the very meaning or its like.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of expressions where metaphorical allusion is used to increase the impact on the listener. Ghazali explains that the thing could be stated explicitly without harm, but it is expressed metaphorically to make a deeper impression. He illustrates with the example of 'pearls on pigs,' where the literal meaning is absurd, prompting the thoughtful person to seek the intended meaning: knowledge given to the unworthy. He then cites a poetic example where a tailor and weaver represent celestial causes of prosperity and decline. Finally, he summarizes that this type involves expressing meaning through an image that contains the same meaning or its equivalent, thus emphasizing the pedagogical utility of metaphor.

Correction: Ghazali shows they serve a specific pedagogical purpose: to increase impact and engage the listener's reflection, as seen in the examples.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Prophetic Examples of Metaphorical Expression
Ghazali provides two hadiths as examples of metaphorical expression in religious texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali uses two prophetic hadiths to illustrate metaphorical expression in religious texts and why literal interpretation is inappropriate.

Core Idea
Metaphorical hadiths convey spiritual lessons, not literal physical events.

In this passage, Ghazali provides concrete examples from the Prophet's sayings to demonstrate the third category of metaphorical expression. These hadiths describe phenomena that cannot be taken literally, such as a mosque shrinking or a head turning into a donkey's head. Ghazali explains the underlying spiritual meaning, showing how metaphor serves to instill reverence and proper conduct. Read the passage and translation, then follow the guided path to unpack the examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice that both hadiths describe actions with physical consequences that are not literally possible.
2
Identify the two hadiths
Find the first hadith about the mosque and sputum, and the second about raising the head before the imam. Note that both are presented as examples of metaphorical speech.
3
Understand Ghazali's explanation of the first hadith
Ghazali clarifies that the mosque does not physically contract; rather, the sanctity of the mosque is metaphorically violated by sputum, causing a spiritual opposition similar to fire on skin.
4
Understand the second hadith's metaphorical meaning
The warning about turning a head into a donkey's head is a metaphor for ignorance or lack of respect, not a literal transformation.
5
Reflect on the purpose of metaphorical language
Consider why the Prophet used such vivid imagery and how it effectively conveys spiritual lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنه قوله : إن المسجد لينزوي من النخامة كما تنزوي الجلدة على النار، وأنت ترى أن ساحة المسجد لا تنقبض بالنخامة . ومعناه أن روح المسجد كونه معظمها ورمی النخامة فيه تحقير له، فيضاد معنى المسجدية مضادة النار لإتصال أجزاء الجلدة. وكذلك قوله : أما يخشى الذي يرفع رأسه قبل الإمام أن يحول الله رأسه رأس حمار.
And from it (i.e., this type) is his saying (peace be upon him): 'The mosque shrinks away from sputum as the skin shrinks over fire.' Yet you see that the courtyard of the mosque does not contract due to sputum. Its meaning is that the spirit of the mosque is its being venerated, and throwing sputum in it is a belittlement of it, so it opposes the meaning of 'mosqueness' just as fire opposes the continuity of the parts of skin. And similarly his saying: 'Does not the one who raises his head before the imam fear that Allah may turn his head into the head of a donkey?'
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage provides two prophetic hadiths as concrete examples of the third category of metaphorical expression. The first hadith states that the mosque 'shrinks away' from sputum like skin from fire. Ghazali explains this is not literal: the mosque does not physically contract, but the spiritual sanctity of the mosque is violated by spitting, creating an opposition analogous to fire's effect on skin. The second hadith warns that raising one's head before the imam may result in Allah turning that head into a donkey's head. Again, this is metaphorical, implying that such behavior reflects ignorance or lack of proper reverence, likening the person to a donkey. Both examples illustrate how metaphorical language conveys powerful spiritual lessons.
