Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
The Salaf's Method of Handling Ambiguous Attributes
Ghazali explains the salaf's approach of passing ambiguous texts without ta'wil, citing Ahmad and Malik.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the salaf's principle of passing ambiguous scriptural texts on divine attributes without interpreting them, and the reasoning behind this approach.

Core Idea
The salaf affirm the meaning, negate the modality, and close the door to speculation.

When faced with Qur'anic and prophetic texts describing Allah in ways that seem anthropomorphic, the early Muslim scholars developed a cautious method. Rather than inventing interpretations, they affirmed the literal wording while leaving the 'how' to Allah. In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali explains this method and its rationale, citing the prominent figures Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Malik ibn Anas.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the names and key terms. Do not worry about every detail yet.
2
Identify the three exceptions
Find the three specific expressions for which some scholars allowed ta'wil (interpretation). Understand why these were considered exceptional.
The expressions involve the Black Stone, the heart of the believer, and the breath from Yemen.
3
Understand the reasoning behind closing the door
Ghazali explains that opening the door to ta'wil leads to uncontrolled speculation. Focus on the phrase 'if the door is opened, the breach widens'.
This is a practical, not doctrinal, reason.
4
Memorize Malik's principle
Imam Malik's famous response when asked about istiwa' summarizes the salaf's method. Commit it to memory: 'Al-istiwa' is known, the modality is unknown.'
This principle applies to all ambiguous attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى سمعت بعض أصحابه يقول : إنه حسم باب التأويل إلا لثلاثة ألفاظ : قوله الحجر الأسود يمين الله في أرضه وقوله قلب المؤمن بين أصبعين من أصابع الرحمن وقوله : « إني لأجد نفس الرحمن من جانب اليمن » المسموعة ، فهو حقيقة فيها مجاز في مدلولها ؛ ونقل عن بعض العلماء أن مذهب أحمد ، أنه تعالى لم يزل متكلماً إذا شاء ومتى شاء ، وكيف شاء ، وهو يتكلم به بصوت يسمع » اهـ

ومال إلى حسم الباب أرباب الظواهر والظن بأحمد بن حنبل رضي الله عنه ، أنه علم ان الإستواء ليس هو الإستقرار والنزول ليس هو الإنتقال ، ولكنه منع من التأويل حسما للباب ، ورعاية الصلاح الخلق ، فإنه إذا فتح الباب اتسع الخرق ، وخرج الأمر مر عن الضبط ، وجاوز حد الإقتصاد اذ حد ما جاوز الإقتصاد لا ينضبط ، فلا بأس بهذا الزجر . ويشهد له سيرة السلف ، فإنهم كانوا يقولون أمروها كما جاءت ، حتى قال مالك رحمه الله لما سئل عن الإستواء : الإستواء معلوم ، والكيفية مجهولة
Until I heard some of his companions saying: He closed the door of interpretation (ta'wil) except for three expressions: his saying 'the Black Stone is the right hand of Allah in His earth', and his saying 'the heart of the believer is between two fingers of the fingers of the Most Merciful', and his saying: 'Truly I find the breath of the Most Merciful from the direction of Yemen' that is heard; so it is literal (haqiqah) in them, metaphorical (majaz) in their referent; and it is transmitted from some scholars that the school of Ahmad is that He, exalted, did not cease to be speaking when He willed, whenever He willed, and however He willed, and He speaks with a voice that is heard. End quote. And the literalists (arbab al-zawahir) inclined to closing the door, and the assumption about Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah be pleased with him, is that he knew that al-istiwa' is not al-istiqrar (settling) and al-nuzul is not al-intiqal (movement), but he prohibited interpretation in order to close the door, and out of care for the reform of the creation; for if the door is opened, the breach widens, the matter becomes difficult to control, and exceeds the limit of moderation (iqtisad), since what exceeds moderation cannot be regulated; so there is no harm in this deterrence. And it is witnessed by the conduct of the predecessors (salaf), for they used to say: 'Pass them on as they came', until Malik, may Allah have mercy on him, said when asked about al-istiwa': 'Al-istiwa' is known, and the modality (kayfiyyah) is unknown.'
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage explains the approach of the salaf (early Muslims) regarding ambiguous scriptural texts about Allah's attributes. It begins by reporting that some companions of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said he 'closed the door of ta'wil' (interpretation) except for three specific expressions: the hadith about the Black Stone as 'the right hand of Allah', the heart of the believer being between two fingers of the Most Merciful, and the 'breath of the Most Merciful from Yemen'. The author notes that these expressions are literal in their wording but metaphorical in their referent. Then it mentions that the school of Ahmad holds that Allah speaks with a voice that is heard. The text then discusses why the 'literalists' inclined to closing the door. It says that Ahmad knew that istiwa' (establishing) is not the same as istiqrar (settling in a place), and nuzul (descending) is not intiqal (spatial movement), but he prohibited ta'wil to close the door for the benefit of the people. The reason is that if ta'wil is allowed, it becomes uncontrolled and exceeds moderation. Then it supports this by citing the practice of the salaf who said 'amiruha kama ja'at' (pass them as they came). Finally, it quotes Malik's famous response when asked about istiwa': 'Al-istiwa' is known, the modality is unknown'. This encapsulates the salaf's method: affirm the attribute without specifying how.

Key Terms
حسم باب التأويل
أمروها كما جاءت
الإستواء
الكيفية مجهولة
ظواهر
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the salaf either rejected all interpretation or that they anthropomorphized attributes.
Correction: In fact, the salaf affirmed the literal wording of the attributes while negating any modal comparison to creation. They did not interpret (ta'wil) but also did not imagine Allah as having physical parts.

Checkpoint
What did Imam Malik say when asked about the meaning of 'istiwa' (establishing) in the verse 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne'?
A) It means sitting on the Throne.
B) It means taking control of the Throne.
C) Al-istiwa' is known, and the modality is unknown.
D) We do not know what it means.

Key Takeaway
The salaf's method is to affirm the literal wording of ambiguous attributes without asking how, trusting in Allah's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about Allah's 'hand' or 'face', does your mind immediately try to explain them in a way that feels safe to your intellect? This lesson calls you to affirm the wording and stop. Are you willing to leave the 'how' unknown, trusting that Allah knows best, or does your pride demand an explanation? What does your reaction reveal about your heart's submission?
?
The salaf closed the door to interpretation for the sake of communal reform, fearing that opening it would lead to uncontrolled speculation. In your personal study of Islam, are there doors of speculation you have opened out of intellectual curiosity or a desire for novelty? Can you identify one such door and commit to closing it, following the salaf's restraint?
?
Imam Malik said, 'Al-istiwa' is known, and the modality is unknown.' Do you truly live with this tension—knowing that you understand the meaning yet cannot comprehend the how? Or do you secretly resent this limitation, wishing for a fully comprehensible deity? Repent of any desire to confine Allah to the grasp of your mind, and embrace the humility of 'pass them as they came.'

Method of Learning
beginner
5 min
The Salaf's Method and Imam Malik's Statement on Istiwa
Ghazali describes the Salaf's method and quotes Malik on istiwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Salaf's approach to ambiguous divine attributes (mutashabihat) and the key principles encapsulated in Imam Malik's famous response about istiwa.

Core Idea
The Salaf affirmed the reality of divine attributes while denying all modality and prohibiting speculative inquiry.

Imam al-Ghazali presents the methodology of the early Muslims (Salaf) as the correct approach to verses about Allah's attributes. Rather than indulging in philosophical interpretation, they would recite the texts as they came, accepting their truth without attempting to explain how. The most famous expression of this method is the response of Imam Malik when asked about Allah's istiwa (establishment over the Throne). In this lesson, we examine Malik's concise yet profound answer, which has become a cornerstone of Sunni creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation to get the wording. Notice the brevity and precision of Malik's four phrases.
2
Understand the Salaf's general principle
Ghazali says the Salaf used to say 'Pass them on as they came.' This means they recited the verses without alteration, denial, or anthropomorphism.
3
Analyze Malik's four-part statement
Malik gives four distinct points: (1) istiwa is known, (2) modality is unknown, (3) belief is obligatory, (4) asking is an innovation. Break down each part.
4
Connect to the broader theological context
Reflect on how this approach avoids both tashbih (likening Allah to creation) and ta'til (denying attributes). This is the balanced position of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشهد له سيرة السلف، فإنهم كانوا يقولون أمروها كما جاءت، حتى قال مالك رحمه الله لما سئل عن الإستواء: الإستواء معلوم، والكيفية مجهولة، والإيمان به واجب، والسؤال عنه بدعة.
And the way of the Salaf bears witness to this, for they used to say: 'Pass them on as they came,' until Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said when asked about al-istiwa: 'Al-istiwa is known, and the modality is unknown, and belief in it is obligatory, and asking about it is an innovation.'
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of the Salaf's method for dealing with ambiguous verses (mutashabihat) concerning Allah's attributes. Ghazali first states that the Salaf's practice (sira) confirms the appropriateness of restraining from interpretation. He quotes their directive: 'Pass them on as they came' (أمروها كما جاءت), meaning they recited the texts without alteration (tahrif), denial (ta'til), likening (tashbih), or modality (takyeef). Then he gives the famous statement of Imam Malik ibn Anas when asked about the meaning of 'istiwa' (Allah's establishment over the Throne). Malik answered with four concise phrases: (1) 'Al-istiwa is known' – affirming that the Arabic word has a real meaning, not that it is meaningless. (2) 'The modality is unknown' – denying that human intellect can grasp how it occurs. (3) 'Belief in it is obligatory' – requiring faith in the attribute as Allah describes it. (4) 'Asking about it is an innovation' – prohibiting speculative inquiry beyond the text. This statement encapsulates the via media of the Salaf: affirming the attribute's reality while negating any comparison to creation and avoiding philosophical speculation.

Key Terms
السلف
التأويل
الاستواء
الكيفية
بدعة
الإيمان
السؤال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Salaf denied the meaning of 'istiwa' entirely or avoided discussing it altogether.
Correction: Malik affirms that istiwa is 'known' (معلوم)—the word has a real meaning that befits Allah—while the modality (how) is unknown. They did not deny the attribute but affirmed it without modality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Imam Malik say about how Allah's istiwa should be understood?
A) It should be interpreted metaphorically as 'dominion'.
B) The meaning is known, the modality is unknown, belief is obligatory, and asking is an innovation.
C) It is a test of faith and should not be discussed at all.
D) It means He sits on the Throne in a physical manner.

Key Takeaway
Imam Malik's four-part statement on istiwa—'the meaning is known, the modality is unknown, belief is obligatory, asking is an innovation'—is a concise expression of the Salaf's balanced approach to divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a verse or hadith about Allah's attributes that you cannot fully grasp, does your heart immediately feel the need to 'figure it out' or do you find peace in accepting it as it came, trusting that its reality is true even if the how is beyond you? Which path brings you closer to Allah, and how will you train your mind to follow the Salaf's way starting today?
?
Imam Malik said that asking about the modality of istiwa is an innovation. Have you ever caught yourself wondering 'how' Allah does something, like how He descends to the lowest heaven or how He is above the Throne? What concrete step will you take this week to stop that line of inquiry and instead focus on affirming the attribute and increasing your awe of Him?
?
The Salaf affirmed the reality of the attribute without knowing the modality. Is your belief in Allah's attributes merely a mental acknowledgment, or does it penetrate your heart so that you truly feel that Allah is al-‘Aliyy (the Most High) over His Throne in a way that befits Him? If you struggle with a particular attribute, what will you do today to strengthen that belief in your heart, knowing that belief in it is obligatory?
